## MMS over MM7

* The **"MM7"** interface enables interactions between "VAS" applications and an "MMSC" and is based on the "Simple Object Access Protocol" (SOAP) with "HTTP" at the "transport" layer. With this configuration, "MM7" request messages are transferred in "HTTP" POST requests, whereas corresponding "MM7" response messages are transferred as part of "HTTP" response messages. 
* **"SOAP"** is a lightweight protocol for the exchange of information in distributed environments such as the "MMSE". A "SOAP" transaction is represented using "XML", and consists of a "SOAP" envelope, a "SOAP" header, a "SOAP" body, and an optional "SOAP" attachment. "MMS" headers are encoded as "XML" document in the "SOAP" header and "SOAP" body. "MMS" content is placed in the "SOAP" attachment encoded as a "MIME" (Multipart Internet Mail Extensions) multipart payload object. "MIME" is used to bundle all of the separate audio, image, and text files together — as well as the base "SMIL" document.
* When a "SOAP" transaction contains a "SOAP" attachment (one or more "MMS" content objects), the **"MIME"** type "multipart/related" is used. This multipart will always consist of exactly two parts, even if the "MMS" message contains more than one content objects. One part is the "text/xml" SOAP "header" and "body", and we’re going to expect to see a "\<Recipients>" section with at least one "\<To>", "\<Cc>" or "\<Bcc>" recipient specified. The other part is a "multipart" object containing the "MMS" content objects. This can be confusing as one multipart object is nested inside another.
* The "Content-Type" at the very top of the message indicates to the receiving client that the separate parts of the message are related and may refer to one another. The boundary is something common to all
multipart messages and indicates to the client what string will separate each of the parts of the message. Normally, the boundary string is a long sequence of random characters with very little likelihood of occurring within a message part. Between each of the boundaries we see the parts of the message. 
* The "MMS" message should always have a **"SMIL"** (Synchronized Multimedia Integration Language) presentation part which determines how the "MMS" message is displayed, and is an "XML" based language. If a "SMIL" presentation is not included in an "MMS" message, many operator "MMS" systems will automatically generate "SMIL" and add it to the message before it is received by the recipient. When included in an "MMS" message, a "SMIL" presentation becomes one of the objects within an "MMS" message. A typical "MMS" message that contains "text" and an "image" would have three objects contained in the "MMS" message, a "SMIL" object, a "text" object (file) and an "image" object (file, e.g. PNG, JPEG, GIF) as in our example that can be found below.
* The entire "SMIL" is enclosed in "\<smil>\</smil>" tags and the message (or document) itself has both "head" and "body" sections. The "head" section contains information that applies to the entire message. The "layout" section within the "head" section specifies the master layout for all the slides in the message. The "layout" section defines two regions in our example. Within the "body" section are the actual slides in the message. These slides are denoted with the "par" tag. "text", "img", "video" and "audio" tags with a "src" parameter define objects that appear in the "MMS" message. The "src" parameter of one of these object tags refers to another content object/filename that is included in the message. Any content referenced by "SMIL" must be a file that is included in the "MMS" message content. If part of the message wishes to refer to another part by "Content-ID" then the scheme "cid:" is used with the reference to that part. Notice that the actual "Content-ID" headers enclose the part’s ID in angle brackets. Generally, "Content-ID" and "Content-Location" are both ways of identifying parts of the message uniquely so that other parts of the message can refer to them. "Content-ID" will always be available for each part of the message. The "dur" attribute for each slide is the duration of the slide in the slide show. There is no in-line text within a "SMIL" presentation. If we want to include "text" in a "SMIL" presentation, we include a reference to a separate "text" object/file.

### MMS over MM7 making use of "curl" 

```
$ curl --verbose --request POST 'http://127.0.0.1:2007/vas' --header 'Content-Transfer-Encoding;' --header 'Content-Type: multipart/related; boundary="==MM7-SOAP==d80baa42-4035-4dd6-9bd0-d880a3ec5557"; type="text/xml"; start="<mm7-soap>"' --header 'MIME-Version;' --header 'SOAPAction:""' --header 'TE;' --header 'X-Mailer;' -H 'Accept:' --data-binary @body.mm7
* Hostname was NOT found in DNS cache
*   Trying 127.0.0.1...
* Connected to 127.0.0.1 (127.0.0.1) port 2007 (#0)
> POST /vas HTTP/1.1
> User-Agent: curl/7.35.0
> Host: 127.0.0.1:2007
> Content-Transfer-Encoding:
> Content-Type: multipart/related; boundary="==MM7-SOAP==d80baa42-4035-4dd6-9bd0-d880a3ec5557"; type="text/xml"; start="<mm7-soap>"
> MIME-Version:
> SOAPAction:""
> TE:
> X-Mailer:
> Content-Length: 150313
> Expect: 100-continue
>
< HTTP/1.1 100 Continue
< HTTP/1.1 200 OK
< Date: Wed, 26 Jan 2022 18:24:52 GMT
< SOAPAction: ""
< Content-Type: text/xml;charset=UTF-8
< Content-Length: 648
< x-huawei-mmsc-tid: 1635347781995
< x-huawei-mmsc-from:
< x-huawei-mmsc-to: 5500000000000
< x-huawei-mmsc-code: 1000
<
* Connection #0 to host 127.0.0.1 left intact
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<soap-env:Envelope xmlns:soap-env="http://schemas.xmlsoap.org/soap/envelope/">
	<soap-env:Header>
		<mm7:TransactionID xmlns:mm7="http://www.3gpp.org/ftp/Specs/archive/23_series/23.140/schema/REL-5-MM7-1-3" soap-env:mustUnderstand="1">1635347781995</mm7:TransactionID>
	</soap-env:Header>
	<soap-env:Body>
		<SubmitRsp xmlns="http://www.3gpp.org/ftp/Specs/archive/23_series/23.140/schema/REL-5-MM7-1-3">
			<MM7Version>6.8.0</MM7Version>
			<Status>
				<StatusCode>1000</StatusCode>
				<StatusText>Sending succeeded.</StatusText>
			</Status>
			<MessageID>0049011012042201261824540405</MessageID>
		</SubmitRsp>
	</soap-env:Body>
</soap-env:Envelope>
$
```

where "body.mm7" is a file with the following format and data :

```
$ cat body.mm7 
--==MM7-SOAP==d80baa42-4035-4dd6-9bd0-d880a3ec5557
Content-Type: text/xml; charset="utf-8"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: binary
Content-ID: <mm7-soap>

<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<env:Envelope xmlns:env="http://schemas.xmlsoap.org/soap/envelope/" xmlns="http://www.3gpp.org/ftp/Specs/archive/23_series/23.140/schema/REL-5-MM7-1-3">
  <env:Header>
    <TransactionID env:mustUnderstand="1">1635347781995</TransactionID>
  </env:Header>
  <env:Body>
    <SubmitReq>
      <MM7Version>6.8.0</MM7Version>
      <SenderIdentification>
        <VASPID>vasp_id</VASPID>
        <VASID>vas_id</VASID>
      </SenderIdentification>
      <Recipients>
        <To>
          <Number>5500000000000</Number>
        </To>
      </Recipients>
      <MessageClass>Advertisment</MessageClass>
      <DeliveryReport>false</DeliveryReport>
      <Priority>Normal</Priority>
      <Subject>MM7 Demo</Subject>	 	  
      <ChargedParty>Neither</ChargedParty>
      <Content allowAdaptations="True" href="cid:mm7-content" />
    </SubmitReq>
  </env:Body>
</env:Envelope>
--==MM7-SOAP==d80baa42-4035-4dd6-9bd0-d880a3ec5557
Content-Type: multipart/related; start="<smil>"; type="application/smil"; boundary="==Multipart==3d8ce4c4-a8b4-4c35-a173-5d8ea55f76e3"
Content-ID: <mm7-content>

--==Multipart==3d8ce4c4-a8b4-4c35-a173-5d8ea55f76e3
Content-Type: application/smil
Content-ID: <smil>
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit

<smil>
	<head>
		<root-layout id="main" width="640px" height="480px">
			<region id="Image" fit="fill" height="100%" width="100%" z-axis="2" />
			<region id="Text" left="0%" width="100%" z-axis="1" />
		</root-layout>
	</head>
	<body>
		<par dur="60000ms">
			<img region="Image" src="cid:image" />
			<text region="Text" src="cid:text" />
		</par>
	</body>
</smil>
--==Multipart==3d8ce4c4-a8b4-4c35-a173-5d8ea55f76e3
Content-Type: image/gif
Content-ID: <image>
Content-Transfer-Encoding: BASE64
```
